          <section
            id="about"
            class="block sidetab-tab active"
            data-tab-target="about"
            data-tab-id="person"
            aria-labelledby="person-about-control"
            role="tabpanel"
          >
            <h2>About</h2>

                                <section class="sidetabs-section mb-25">
  <div>
<p>Dr. David Millard is Professor of Computer Science at the <a href="https://www.ecs.soton.ac.uk">University of Southampton, Electronics and Computer Science, UK</a>. He has been an active member of the international hypermedia community for over twenty five years, firstly in the area of Open and Adaptive hypermedia and later working with Social Media Analytics, Digital Narratives, and Web Science.</p>
</div>
<div>
<p>David is the Head of the ECS Education Group at Southampton, where he leads a team of 15 Teaching Fellows and Senior Fellows, with a remit to improve teaching and learning across the department. David was previously the Director of Admissions for ECS (from 2012 to 2022), leading the schools admissions strategy and taking responsibility for all undergraduate, postgraduate taught, and post-graduate research admisions activities (such as Open and Visit days).&nbsp;</p>
<p>David is also a founding member of the <a href="https://www.wais.ecs.soton.ac.uk">Web and Internet Science research group</a>, was vice-chair of <a href="https://www.sigweb.org">ACM SIGWEB</a> (the ACM Special Interest Group on the Web) from 2015-2019, and is the current <a href="https://ht.acm.org">Chair of the ACM Hypertext steering committee</a> as well as the SIGWEB Liaison for <a href="https://webscience.org">ACM Web Science</a>.&nbsp;He has been a programme committee member for over 35 conference events, including ACM CHI, Web Science, SocInfo, and IEEE ICALT, as well as ACM Hypertext and ICIDS where he also served as the Programme Chair (in 2019 and 2020 respectively). David also serves on the editorial board of the <a href="https://www.tandfonline.com/journals/tham20">New Review of Hypermedia</a>, published by Taylor and Francis.</p>
<p>David is the co-founder of the <a href="http://nht.ecs.soton.ac.uk/">Narrative and Hypertext workshop</a> that has been running since 2011, and in 2022 co-edited <a href="https://link.springer.com/book/9783031052132">`The Authoring Problem' published by Springer</a>, containing chapters on Interactive Digital Narrative Authoring theory and tools by leading international researchers.&nbsp;</p>
<p>He leads a team of PhD students focused on Interactive Narratives and Mixed Reality Spaces, and has previously graduated 34 postgraduate students working in these areas as well as Web Science and e-learning. Many of these students have studied interdisciplinary topics, and he frequently co-supervises with colleagues from other departments, this has included Law, Social Sciences, English, History, Geography, Politics, Education, Film, Psychology, and the WSA. David's students have gone on to varied careers in academia and industry including major technology firms such as IBM and Google, and academic positions in the UK (Oxford, Winchester, Bournemouth, and East Anglia), Malaysia, Pakistan, and Saudi Arabia.&nbsp;He has been the external PhD examiner for 9 theses, including students at the Universities of KCL, Lisbon, Trinity College, Manchester, and Nottingham. He has twice been nominated for a Vice-Chancellers Award for his PhD supervision, and in 2020 his student Sifia Kitomilli won the best newcomer award for her research published at ACM Hypertext.</p>
</div>
</section>

          <section
            id="research"
            class="block sidetab-tab hidden"
            data-tab-target="research"
            data-tab-id="person"
            aria-labelledby="person-research-control"
            role="tabpanel"
          >
            <h2>Research</h2>

            
                                
<section class="sidetabs-section">
      <h3>Research groups</h3>
    <div id="research-groups-membership-list">Member of:
    <ul class="mt-2">
              <li class="list-arrow pb-2"><a href="/research/institutes-centres/web-internet-science" target="_blank">Web and Internet Science</a></li>
              <li class="list-arrow pb-2"><a href="/research/groups/ecs-education-group" target="_blank">ECS Education Group</a></li>
          </ul>
    </div>
        <h3>Research interests</h3>
    <ul>
                <li class="list-arrow pb-2">Hypertext Systems</li>
                <li class="list-arrow pb-2">Interactive Digital Narratives </li>
                <li class="list-arrow pb-2">Mixed Reality Games</li>
          </ul>
        <h3>Current research</h3>
    <p>David has been involved in Hypertext and Web research for over twenty five years, firstly in the area of Open, Adaptive and Contextual hypermedia and later&nbsp;the areas of Social Media Analytics, Linked Data, UX Design, Web Science, and Interactive Digital Narrative. He spent a number of years applying this sort of technology to&nbsp;e-learning, in particular digital literacy, personal-learning systems, and open educational resources&nbsp;(OER). His current research interests are based around hypertext, digital narratives and mixed reality games, in particular locative literature.</p>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<p>David has authored more than 230 peer-reviewed articles across the areas of Technology Enhanced Learning, Web Science, and Hypertext and Narrative. This includes research published in prestigious journals such as Springer Multimedia Tools and Applications, Elsevier Computers in Education, IEEE Intelligent Systems, PloS one, ACM Transactions on Information Systems, and ACM Transactions on Learning Technologies. Google Scholar reports more than 4800 citations of his work, with a h-index of 35.</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>David is interested in the overlap between Hypertext, Games, and Interactive Digital Narratives (IDNs) especially the structural models and patterns they use, and how this relates to the interactivity within the narrative, and the challenges of authoring it in the first place.&nbsp;His work has helped to define the area of Sculptural Hypertext (hypertext governed by rules and constraints rather than navigational links), a modelling approach that is highly suitable for conceptualising and designing narrative structures within digital games. He has also worked extensively on locative narratives, interactive digital narrative games that are experienced on location-aware smart devices, and was one of the very first people to work on this area (through his work on located stories and games as Chawton House, from 2002). Recently this has focused on understanding the locative narrative design space, where David has been working towards a design framework for successful locative experiences, and proposed the&nbsp;<em><a href="https://eprints.soton.ac.uk/444357/">Balance of Attention</a>&nbsp;</em>as the primary poetic of locative narrative.</p>
<p>David is proud to be a double-award winner of the <a href="http://www.sigweb.org/resources/sigweb-awards/44-douglas-engelbart">Engelbart Award</a>&nbsp;(2013, 2016) for his work on location-based storytelling and sculptural hypertext – exploring how digital narratives can be interwoven with real-world places. This is best exemplified by <a href="http://storyplaces.soton.ac.uk/">StoryPlaces</a>, an interdisciplinary research project working with writers to explore the poetics of location-based narratives through digital&nbsp;storytelling deployments&nbsp;in Southampton, Bournemouth, and Crystal Palace.</p>
        <h3>Research projects</h3>
    <div class="mb-25">

          <section
            id="teaching"
            class="block sidetab-tab hidden"
            data-tab-target="teaching"
            data-tab-id="person"
            aria-labelledby="person-teaching-control"
            role="tabpanel"
          >
            <h2>Teaching</h2>

            
            
            
            
                                <section class="sidetabs-section mb-25">
  <div>
<div>
<div>
<div>
<p>David has a long and established record of leading, undertaking, and publishing pedagogic projects and research in e-learning in a range of international peer reviewed conferences and journals. In total he has around 70 publications in Technology Enhanced Learning, with topics including Open Educational Resources (OER), Learning Analytics, Automatic Group formation, Personal Learning Environments, and Digital Assessment Tools. His work in OER has been published in the two leading journals of the field: IEEE Transactions on Learning Technologies, and Elsevier Computers in Education. In 2017 he gave a keynote talk at the conference of the European Association of Computer Assisted Language Learning (Eurocall) on the dangers presented by social media personalisation and data harvesting for Technology Enhanced Learning.</p>
<p>David has been a pioneer of Open Educational Resources, and through a series of JISC projects developed EdShare in 2010, on OER platform based on EPrints, which took a revolutionary Web 2.0 approach to learning objects. EdShare Southampton has now been running at the University for 10 years and has been widely adopted (it now hosts over 20,000 learning items deposited by teaching staff across the institution). He has also worked directly with other organisations to establish OER repositories for their own communities, and in 2012 oversaw the transfer of EdShare support to EPrints Services, where it continues to be developed and maintained. EdShare has had substantial impact on the way that OER has been viewed within the UK and is used by a wide variety of higher educational institutions, including the Open University, and the University of Glasgow.</p>
<p>Within ECS David has a track record of innovative pedagogical approaches (for example, basing the structure of modules on student conferences, dragon’s den activities, or GameJam events), including a third-year BSc course on Multimedia Systems (COMP3013) that won the Vice-Chancellor’s Teaching award. He led the key Programming 1 module (COMP1202) for more than a decade, one of the largest and most complex modules in ECS supporting over 300 students each year through three separate streams of teaching, and he has proposed, developed and led new modules on <em>Social Media and Network Science</em> (COMP6217/COMP6250); and more recently <em>Games Design and Development</em> (COMP3218).</p>
<p>In addition to his University teaching David was part of the original Southampton team engaged with the FutureLearn initiative and I helped to develop MOOC pedagogy within the University, contributing to both the process of production and the design philosophy for learning activities. The University's first MOOC,<em> Web Science: How the Web is Changing the World</em>, has run with thousands of online students (the largest single cohort was more than 12,000 people) and as one of the first UK courses of its type featured on BBC Radio 4’s Today Programme. This experience resulted in David being invited to develop and produce courses for the Southampton Data Science Academy (<em>Data Science for Digital Marketing</em>, and <em>AI and Machine Learning for Business</em>).</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
  
</section>
